After Japanese Troops Bombed Tianjin 124

Shanghai-Tianjin Transportation Obstructed

Chinese Ships Suspended

Japanese Troops Bombed Chinese Territory in Tianjin Again. Yesterday morning, the Shanghai shipping companies received telegrams from Tianjin warning that Tianjin was in chaos and business had completely stopped. Only the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company's Xinming and Xinfeng ships were operating regular services on the Shanghai-North China route. Yesterday, the company's Xinming ship was ordered to go to Japan, and the Xinfeng ship was also temporarily suspended from going to Tianjin. The other shipping companies also sent telegrams to the temporary cargo ships going to North China, stating that if the situation in Tianjin was dangerous, they could stop going and go to other ports to anchor for safety. Those that had not yet departed were stopped. Yesterday, the Shanghai-Tianjin Chinese ships had suspended operations.

Japanese Ships Stopped

After the Tianjin chaos occurred, the Shanghai-based Japanese shipping companies Osaka and Nisshin received telegrams from the Japanese authorities in Tianjin, stating that the Japanese ships Chang'an Maru, Henan Maru, Huashan Maru, and others that had arrived in Tianjin had been detained by the Japanese authorities. After the goods and passengers were unloaded, the commercial services were suspended. Goods and passengers were refused boarding. They are currently staying in Tianjin to provide accommodation for Japanese residents in Tianjin, and when necessary, they will be used to transport Japanese residents to Dalian. Japanese ships sailing en route have been escorted by Japanese warships dispatched from Qingdao. Japanese ships in North China are still recklessly colliding.

Goods Interrupted

The time when large quantities of flour, piece goods, and groceries were being transported to North China, yesterday suddenly announced an interruption. Goods from Tianjin to Shanghai had been completely stopped. After the Shanghai export goods were urgently telegraphed to stop shipping by the Tianjin group yesterday, a large number of goods that had been declared but not yet loaded were temporarily stopped from loading yesterday afternoon. Those that had not been declared were temporarily ordered to be stored in the Shanghai warehouse and not shipped. North-south transportation has been severely hit. It is said that the foreign ships that had already departed have used warships to protect them and unloaded the goods into the Tanggu warehouse, unable to directly reach the Zizhu Forest area.

Oppose Establishing Neutral Zone

The name of a neutral zone is established, and the reality is common management. The members of this group take anti-Japanese and national salvation as their mission. We hereby circulate the resolution of the Provisional Committee, wishing all compatriots and groups across the country to unanimously advocate and join forces against Japan. We must know that the day the neutral zone is realized is the day the Eastern Provinces are openly divided. Our people should rise up and urge the League of Nations to insist on its September 30 resolution ordering Japan to withdraw its troops and to take effective sanctions under Article 16 of the Covenant due to Japan's exceeding the deadline. We are at a loss and filled with indignation.

Public Association of Silver and Money Industries 128

Pay Attention to the Export of Silver Dollars

Money Industry Association Believes a Ban on Export is Impossible

Banking Association to Discuss in Today's Regular Meeting

Qin Runqing and Lin Kanghou Both Make Statements

The recent unusual tightness of money in this city, along with the large-scale export of silver dollars, has attracted the attention of various sectors. The Municipal Chamber of Commerce, in order to prevent this, sent letters to both the silver and money industries, seeking advice on measures. The Money Industry Anti-Japanese National Salvation Association has resolved to form an investigation team to thoroughly investigate and advise the Customs Brokers Association not to handle exports to avoid financial panic. The details of the various situations are recorded separately below:

Export Situation: The silver dollars in this city are minted by the Hangzhou Mint, producing 360,000 yuan per day, contracted by the Bank of China, Bank of Communications, and other banks. In recent days, the money supply has been unusually tight. For example, on the 26th, the difference between the morning and afternoon silver exchange rates was more than 2%, whereas normally it is only about 0.25%. The reason is the large-scale export of silver dollars in recent days, while the import of large bars of silver has slightly decreased compared to before. For example, exporting 10,000 silver dollars can earn hundreds of yuan for Chinese exchange firms, and 40 to 50 yuan for banks and money shops. Therefore, the Japanese are using high profits to entice Chinese merchants to absorb silver dollars. To avoid attracting attention, they are first transported to Tianjin, Qingdao, and Yantai, and then transferred to Dalian and the Northeast. A few Chinese merchants, greedy for small profits, are unaware of their plot and are falling into their trap. If they do not realize this soon, then this city will directly suffer the panic of a shortage of silver dollars, and indirectly, the domestic financial market will be disrupted. It is said that the Japanese are absorbing silver dollars for the purpose of using them in the Northeast and elsewhere to entice bandits to cause trouble.

Money Industry Meeting: The Money Industry Association received a letter from the Municipal Chamber of Commerce yesterday, seeking advice on preventive measures. They then convened a temporary executive committee meeting at the Ningbo Road Association at 1:00 PM. Those present included Pei Yunqing, Wang Juru, Sheng Xiaoshan, Qin Runqing, Wang Bochen, Li Shoushan, Li Jisheng, Yan Junan, and Fu Songnian. After a report by Chairman Qin Runqing, discussions began regarding the case of transporting silver dollars to the North. It was reportedly decided that: (1) The transport of silver dollars by Chinese firms is solely for the purpose of relieving financial panic in other ports and has no other purpose, so an absolute ban on exports is practically impossible; (2) Respond to the Municipal Chamber of Commerce's letter for review; (3) Immediately contact the Banking Association to discuss measures.

Qin Runqing's Remarks: A reporter from the Newsound Society visited Qin Runqing, chairman of the Money Industry Association, yesterday and asked for his opinion on the large-scale export of silver dollars. He said that the export of silver dollars is a very common and legitimate business for the silver and money industries. Moreover, the silver dollars transported to Tianjin, Qingdao, and Yantai this time were purely purchased by Chinese merchants in those areas, with the sole purpose of adjusting the financial situation and no other purpose. Since the Tianjin Incident, people have been panicking, fearing problems with paper money, and are storing silver dollars to prepare for the worst. If the Japanese want to absorb silver dollars, they can simply export them through Japanese banks in this city without having to go through Chinese hands.

Lin Kanghou's Remarks: A reporter from the Newsound Society also visited Lin Kanghou, Secretary-General of the Banking Association, yesterday and asked for his opinion on the export of silver dollars. He said that since the Tianjin Incident, financial panic has arisen in Tianjin. To adjust the situation, the banking community in this city transported over 3 million yuan to the Bank of China in Tianjin, over 1 million yuan to the Bank of Communications, and a total of approximately 5 million yuan to other banks last week, with no other purpose. Moreover, a ban on the export of silver dollars is practically difficult to implement. For example, the recent donations from various sectors to reward General Ma Zhanshan amounted to about one million yuan, all remitted from banks in Shanghai to Harbin, and must be accompanied by the export of silver dollars to adjust the situation; otherwise, financial panic will inevitably occur in Harbin. It is also possible that some wealthy individuals are withdrawing deposits from Shanghai and remitting them to Tianjin, then transferring them to Dalian to exchange for gold coins and deposit them in banks. The Banking Association has received a letter from the Municipal Chamber of Commerce and has scheduled a detailed discussion at the Association's regular meeting at 2:00 PM tomorrow.

Advice to Stop Transportation: The Shanghai Money Industry Anti-Japanese National Salvation Association issued a notice yesterday stating, "Notice: Since the preparation of this Association, we have received enthusiastic participation from all those with ambition and the approval of the Executive Committee of this industry. Therefore, last night (26th), we held a members' inaugural meeting and resolved to strictly implement the five proposals passed by the 19th regular meeting of the industry and to advise all colleagues to voluntarily stop transporting cash to Dalian, Yantai, Yingkou, Tianjin, Qingdao, and other places. This matter concerns national salvation, and we sincerely hope that all colleagues will act in good faith. This is our earnest hope. Sincerely, The Shanghai Money Industry Anti-Japanese National Salvation Association, November 27th."

Foreign Press Reports 129

Situation of Boycotting Japanese Goods

Japanese Economist Says Decline Imminent

Will Chinese Merchants Endure the Mockery of "Five-Minute Enthusiasm"?

The North China Daily News' Tokyo correspondent reported on the 15th that the Chinese people's boycott of Japanese goods has dealt a major blow to Japan. According to newspaper reports, Japanese residents in various parts of China, especially those in Shanghai, are on the verge of bankruptcy. It is reported that the Shanghai Bureau of Industry and Commerce is importing Manchester yarn and sheeting to meet the shortage of goods in the market after the boycott of Japanese goods, and various anti-Japanese groups are intensifying their efforts to sever economic and commercial relations with Japan. According to reports here, Japanese goods have been piled up in the warehouses of Nippon Yusen Kaisha alone, totaling 36,500 tons, and it is feared that there will be no hope of shipment in several months. The sharp decline in Japanese goods exported to China can be evidenced by the Asosan Maru, which recently arrived in Shanghai. The ship only carried 150 tons of cargo, all for Japanese merchants. It is said that small Japanese merchants and capitalists in Shanghai have no other choice but bankruptcy. Among the 40 smaller Japanese factories in the area, each employing about 30 workers, no fewer than 33 have been forced to close. Half of the Japanese-owned shops in Shanghai are unable to pay their employees' salaries, and half of the Japanese workers in Shanghai have returned home. It is expected that Japanese-owned yarn factories in China will soon close down. At that time, Chinese workers will no longer be paid severance, which may lead to disputes. There are 40 Japanese-owned yarn factories in China, with a total of 1,655,000 spindles and 13,090 looms, with a total investment of approximately 200,000,000 Japanese yen. Among them, 27 are located in Shanghai, with 1,169,000 spindles and 9,900 looms. Although the major Japanese textile factories in Shanghai have not yet closed down, it is only a matter of time before they cease operations. Several famous Japanese economists predict that the future of the boycott of Japanese goods in Shanghai will be decided within the next one or two months. In the past, the boycott of Japanese goods often subsided when Chinese merchants had used up their stock of Japanese goods. It is now expected that this stock of Japanese goods will also be exhausted in one month or six weeks, at which time there will be a battle between money and patriotism, and the decline or not of the boycott of Japanese goods will be decided at this time. However, according to the opinion of Takayanagi, secretary of the Osaka Chamber of Commerce, this boycott is very well organized, and even if its momentum slightly declines, the overall impact on Japan may not be reduced. At present, trade between Japan and central and southern China has completely stopped, and even in northern China and the Northeast, it has greatly decreased compared to normal.

New Ming Vessel to Japan to Pick Up Overseas Chinese 130

Departure Possible in Two Days

New Feng May Not Go Again

The China Merchants Steam Navigation Company received an order from the Ministry of Communications to dispatch a ship to Japan to pick up overseas Chinese returning home. Commissioner Guo Waifeng selected the New Ming, the fastest vessel, for the trip. If necessary, the New Feng would also sail east. It is now known that there are only over 1,000 overseas Chinese in Kobe, Osaka, Yokohama, and other places who are unable to return home. The New Ming can carry over 1,300 people, so it has been decided that the New Feng will not sail again. The New Ming arrived in Shanghai from Tianjin at 8:00 AM yesterday and docked at the Jinliyuan Wharf in the French Concession. It is scheduled to sail to Yokohama on the 30th. Because the Bureau has never had a wharf in Japan, it sent a letter to the Dalai Shipping Company on Wuma Road yesterday, asking them to serve as the New Ming's Yokohama agent. At the same time, it also sent a letter to the Shanghai branch of Yamashita Kisen Co., Ltd. at 56 Sichuan Road, asking them to hire a pilot. As for food and fuel, everything has been prepared. A special license has also been issued by the Ministry of Communications to the Jianghai Customs. The New Ming is the latest type of vessel of the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company, 270 feet long, with a displacement of 2,133 tons, and a speed of 12 nautical miles per hour.

Li Jingcong Talks About 142

The Preparation of the Northwest Aviation Route

Trial Flight on the 10th of Next Month, Formal Flights in the Spring

In the Future, the Europe-Asia Line Will Also Reach This Route Directly

Li Jingcong, Director of the Eurasia Aviation Corporation, went to Beiping to prepare for the Northwest Route and has now completed preparations. He returned to Shanghai the night before last. A reporter from the Newsound Society visited Mr. Li at the company yesterday and asked about everything concerning the Northwest Route. Mr. Li spoke in detail, saying that the trial flight has been scheduled for the 10th of next month and that formal flights may be possible around March of next year. At that time, the Europe-Asia Line (i.e., Shanghai to Berlin, Germany) can also be reached directly via the Northwest Route, which is more convenient than detouring through Manchuria. The following is a record of his conversation:

Preparation Process: Mr. Li talked about the preparation process in three points: (1) Regarding the investigation of climate, because the weather in the Northwest is very cold, cold-proof equipment has been prepared for the aircraft parts. The first and second months of the lunar calendar are very cold and difficult to fly. There are no major problems during the rest of the period; (2) Regarding the transportation of gasoline, gasoline is the most important item for flight. It has now been decided that gasoline will be transported from Beiping to various stations. The oil for the Dihua station will be purchased from Russia because the area is close to Russia; (3) Regarding the equipment on the aircraft, such as cold-proof equipment and in-flight drinks and fuel, very good solutions have been obtained.

Surveying Air Stations: Regarding the establishment of air stations, they have now been surveyed. There are a total of five stations from Beiping to Dihua, namely Beiping, Bailin Temple (Hebei), Ruoshui River (Suiyuan), Hami (Ningxia), Dihua (Xinjiang). Xinjiang, passing through the borders of four provinces, a distance of over 1,700 kilometers, equivalent to over 3,000 Chinese miles. Rumors that it must pass through the provinces of Rehe, etc., are inaccurate. These five stations are the shortest route from Ping to Di.

Definite Date for Trial Flight: The trial flight date has now been set for the 10th of next month after the preparations have been completed. This time, he and Mr. Schmidt prepared in Beijing for more than two weeks. It is difficult for them to come to Shanghai and they must go to Ping again at the end of this month or the beginning of next month to preside over the trial flight because further delays will mean that the severe winter will arrive, making it even more difficult to determine the official flight date. However, it must be around February or March of the lunar calendar next year.

Aircraft Issue: As for the aircraft that will fly the Northwest Route, because the company has many aircraft, it does not plan to purchase any more from foreign countries. The aircraft for this trial flight will be the latest type of Junkers W 33.

Europe-Asia Shortcut: The Eurasia Line planned by the company runs from Shanghai to Berlin, Germany, passing through Jingping, Linxi, Manchuria, and the Russian cities of Irkutsk, Moscow, etc., before reaching Berlin. Previously, flights were suspended because an aircraft mistakenly entered Outer Mongolia and was detained, and has not yet been returned, causing great losses. Now, because Jubei has been forcibly occupied by the Japanese, there is no hope of resuming flights. If the Northwest Route is opened, the Shanghai-Berlin line can take a shortcut through the Northwest without passing through Linxi, Manchuria, etc., and can go directly from Shanghai to Ping to Di, cross the Russian border and reach Berlin, which is much faster than before. The journey from Beiping to Dihua takes more than two months. With the establishment of the Northwest Line, it will only take 12 hours for the aircraft to arrive.

Substitute Materials for Japanese Cotton Textile Raw Materials 143

English Yarn Already Shipped to Shanghai

First Batch of Over 340 Pieces

Original Price of 484 Taels of Silver Per Piece

Since the silk mercerized cotton textile industry in this city unanimously refused to purchase Japanese yarn, the domestic yarn market has become active again. However, due to the imbalance between supply and demand, there is a sudden fear of a shortage of cotton textile raw materials. The Municipal Bureau of Social Affairs and the Municipal Party Department have convened various related groups to discuss the method of ordering English yarn as a substitute for Japanese yarn, but there has been no good result so far. However, the cotton textile factories with greater capital, after receiving the instruction from the Bureau of Social Affairs to replace Japanese yarn with English yarn, immediately telegraphed directly to Manchester, England, to order large quantities of English yarn for supply. The first batch of orders totaled over 340 pieces. Some of them have already been shipped to Shanghai yesterday and were imported by Best & Co. and Jardine Matheson, two foreign firms in this city, as agents. The English yarn is Green Head, Sudan trademark, with specifications of 40s, 80s, and 32s. The original price is 484 taels of silver per piece. Because its quality is comparable to that of Japanese goods, it is very suitable for use in cotton textiles.

Railway Ministry's Measures to Relieve the Coal Shortage 145

Will Organize a National Coal Transport Committee

Since the coal shortage has been felt in this city and the upper and lower reaches of the Yangtze River, the Ministry of Industry, at the request of various coal merchants, held a meeting a few days ago to discuss relief measures. In addition to representatives from various coal merchants, the Railway Ministry also sent Guan Genglin, Director of the Business Department, to participate in the discussions. Now that the meeting has concluded, Director Guan came to Shanghai yesterday on official business. A reporter from the Xin Sheng News Agency interviewed him. The main points of the conversation are recorded below: (Q) What were the results of Director Guan's attendance at the Ministry of Industry's meeting to relieve the coal shortage? (A) At this time, I was ordered by the Ministry to attend the Ministry of Industry's meeting to relieve the coal shortage and reported in detail on the Ministry's plans for transporting national coal. Representatives from all parties expressed satisfaction. (Q) I heard that the monthly coal consumption in the upper and lower reaches of the Yangtze River is huge. How will it be supplied? (A) The annual coal consumption in the Yangtze River area is about four million tons. In addition to supplying a portion of the coal produced in places such as Kai Luan and Qingdao, the meeting hoped that the Ministry would transport 1.2 million tons annually on the Tianjin-Pukou and Beijing-Hankou Railways, averaging 100,000 tons per month, to make up for the shortage. Currently, the Tianjin-Pukou Railway has 13 special coal trains, which can transport an average of 4,500 tons per month. In addition, with the allocation from the Beining and Longhai Railways, there will be 20 trains, which can transport 90,000 tons per month. The Beijing-Hankou Railway transports coal from Liuhegou, which can reach 20,000 tons per month, making a total of 110,000 tons per month. (Q) I heard that your Ministry is considering organizing a special supervisory body to urge coal transport. Is that true? (A) Yes, because coal is a bulky cargo and the freight rate is low, sometimes not even covering the cost. From a railway business perspective, it is not as profitable as transporting other goods. However, in order to actively alleviate the coal shortage, the Ministry will organize a National Coal Transport Committee, formulate measures to allocate vehicles from various railways, and directly command them to alleviate the coal shortage, so as to ensure a steady supply. (Q) Does your Ministry rely solely on rail transport for transporting coal, or do you also handle combined water and land transport? (A) The shortage of domestic ships is even more severe than the shortage of vehicles. In the Pukou area, there are currently over 30,000 tons of coal that have been transported there, but they cannot be shipped due to a lack of ships. Tanggu, Qingdao, and other places are also experiencing this problem. The Ministry has consulted with the Ministry of Communications to quickly find a way to allocate ships to facilitate combined water and land transport. According to the Ministry of Communications' reply, it has telegraphed the Shanghai Maritime Affairs Bureau to quickly consult with Shanghai shipping companies to charter ships for transport. The Ministry has also instructed the Tianjin-Pukou Railway Bureau to actively renovate the Pukou docks to prepare for the berthing of large ships.

Xin Zha Road 147

Another Corpse Dug Up Yesterday

Buried One Zhang Deep Underground

The Corpse Dug Up the Day Before Yesterday Was Female

Digging Must Continue Today

Since the occurrence of the Communist Party's killing and burial to eliminate traces in this city, the French Concession Police and the Public Concession Police have successively dug up eleven male and female corpses in Aitang Village on Yaozhu Jiao Road and No. 6 Xiude Lane on Wuding Road. The details have been recorded in this newspaper. On the 26th of this month, the police continued to dig up a corpse in House A, No. 91 Chenjia Lane, Xin Zha Road. It was said that the name was Zhu Wanbai, who was killed by the Communist Party and buried in the house. The details were seen in yesterday's newspaper. Yesterday morning, Guo Wei, Prosecutor of the First Special District Local Court, accompanied by Clerk Liu Chun and Forensic Doctor Wei Ligong, went to No. 91 Chenjia Lane to investigate. According to the inspection, the corpse dug up was a female corpse. The name has not yet been found. It was not Zhu Wanbai's corpse. At that time, it was learned that there were four more corpses buried in the house, and they needed to be excavated continuously. Therefore, after Mr. Guo inspected it once, he ordered that after all the corpses were dug up, they should be sent to the Feilun Road Corpse Inspection Office for re-examination.

Also, starting at eight o'clock yesterday morning, the personnel of the Department of Justice and others, together with the Public Concession Police, continued to work at the original excavation site. They were busy for half a day, but at first there was nothing to gain. It was not until around three o'clock in the afternoon that a male corpse was dug up below the third excavation site the day before yesterday. The burial place was as deep as one zhang or more, so the excavation was very difficult. The direction of its location was the northwest corner of the courtyard. The corpse was tied with ropes all over the body, similar to the one obtained the day before yesterday. However, it was buried flat in the soil, and rope strangulation was also seen on the neck. According to personnel at the scene, it was speculated that this corpse may be Huang Di Hong. As for the one dug up the day before yesterday, as mentioned above, it was a female corpse, or it may be Zou Zhishu. Because all the corpses were extremely decayed, it was difficult to identify them at once. It is said that the female corpse dug up the day before yesterday had very long hair on her head, and she was also quite young. She was wearing shorts and slippers, seemingly in summer attire. Corpses have been searched for and dug up for days. As of yesterday, a total of thirteen bodies have been found in the British and French concessions. Digging must continue at the original location today. According to eyewitnesses, the necks of all the corpses that have been found have rope strangulation marks, and what is strange is that the knots on the ropes are all the same.

Zhao Shan Executed by Several Gunshots

Zhao's Last Words: Educate His Younger Brother Well

Because of the People He Befriended, Gen Would Not Have a Good Death

Zhao Shan, a native of Haimen, 23 years old, led a group with hidden daggers to Zhao Genchang's house in Baijiazhai, Pingliang Road, to rob at 11:30 p.m. on May 31 this year, and shot and killed one person named Yin Yuanyuan, and also shot and wounded Zhao's wife, Zhang, in the right breast. After the case occurred, the Huishi Police Station arrested him and handed him over to the First Special Court, which sentenced Liang to seven years in prison. The police station refused to accept and appealed. After questioning by the High Court, the sentence was changed to death. It was submitted to the Jiangsu Provincial Government for approval and scheduled for execution. Yesterday afternoon, Cheng Shangfeng, the execution judge of the First Court, took his seat in the Criminal Court No. 3 and brought the appellant to the case. After questioning by the High Court, the sentence was changed to death. It was submitted to the Jiangsu Provincial Government for approval and scheduled for execution. Yesterday afternoon, Cheng Shangfeng, the execution judge of the First Court, took his seat in the Criminal Court No. 3, ordered the prisoner to be brought to the case, and asked if he had any last words. According to Zhao's confession, he requested a letter to be sent to his sister Shen Zhao at No. 15 Huade Road, Gao郎 Bridge, asking her to comfort his mother and telling her not to worry. There was nothing else to say. Judge Cheng then ordered him to be escorted to the local court for execution. The police escorted the prisoner onto a car and drove to the Caohejing execution ground. Zhao Zikui, a prosecutor from the Shanghai Local Court, was appointed as the supervising official. He immediately ordered Police Chief Xu Jinqing, Police Officer Chen Xihui, and supervising execution police Xue Bingzhang, Wang Jianqing, Yin Daoxu, and Zhang Chunsen to go to the execution ground. The judge then accompanied Warden Dong and Clerk Zhang to their official positions and ordered Zhao Shan to be brought to the case. He confessed that he was 23 years old, a native of Haimen, lived on Huade Road in Shanghai, and worked as a handyman. He requested that a letter be written on his behalf to his father Zhao Jintang at Dasheng No. 3 Factory, Qinglong Port, Waisha, asking him to collect the body. He also told his father to educate his younger brother well and strive for progress. Because he lacked education and befriended bandits, he would not have a good death, and so on. The judge then ordered the execution. Police Chief Xu directed the police to take him away and execute him by shooting. After the forensic examiner verified, he ordered the court to collect the body and issue a sealed coffin for collection.

Real Estate Will Be Auctioned

Huang Chujiu previously rented a house on Zhejiang Road from a certain surname for 72,000 taels per year, plus a land tax of about 78,000 taels. Huang Chujiu then mortgaged this rental property to the Tonghui Company for a total of 210,000 taels. The house lost more than 4,000 taels per month. Since Huang's death, Tonghui Company has paid the land rent and other expenses on its behalf, amounting to more than 80,000 taels. This time, the rent payment period has arrived again. Tonghui Company has entrusted someone to repeatedly beg the owner to temporarily suspend the payment. Therefore, it is necessary to urgently request a quick resolution. If it is delayed any longer, once it is unconditionally taken back by the owner, both parties will suffer huge losses and a great danger will definitely occur. Yan Luqing and Xu Yannian, the representatives of the creditors, and their lawyers also stated that this issue must be carefully reviewed by the creditors before being included in the auction. Judge Wang ordered that the case had been pending for a long time and that the accountants Pan and Wu should expedite the auction of Huang's property at the highest price. At this point, it was past noon, and the court adjourned.

City Public Works Bureau Handles 153

Renewal of Permits for Water Supply Equipment Self-Installed by Property Owners

From the Beginning of Next Month to the End of the Month

Failure to Renew the Permit on Time Will Be Subject to Punishment

The City Public Works Bureau has registered 440 places in the city where owners have self-installed water supply equipment. For the convenience of inspection and rectification, the bureau has issued a permit to each place for water use. The permit was originally scheduled to be renewed every year. However, since the owners received the permits at different times, it would be difficult to remember the dates and renew them on time. Therefore, with the approval of the municipal government, it was designated that the period from December 1st to 31st every year would be the permit renewal period for self-installed water supply equipment. Those who received the permit for less than six months can renew it for free. Those who have received the permit for more than six months but less than one year will be charged half the fee of half a yuan. It is now known that the bureau has scheduled to handle the renewal of permits for this term starting on December 1st. However, if the owners have not renewed their permits by the end of December, they will be charged an additional 20% of the permit renewal fee for each day of delay as a penalty for overdue renewal.

Shi Jiulin, a native of Yuyao, 30 years old, who lived in the kitchen shed at No. 14 Xingyi Lane, Lagenna Road (Huanghe Road), French Concession, was previously a tailor of iron carts. After losing his job, he became a hawker, selling pork during the day and shouting and selling olives in a bag at night. In the early summer of this year, he married a woman named Lou (21 years old) from Ningbo as his wife. The couple depended on each other for a living. Recently, due to a lack of capital and financial difficulties, he had a suicidal thought. At about 5 p.m., his wife returned home, knocked on the door but did not respond. She called the second landlord, Shi Zhuqing, to pry open the door and entered the house before discovering it. Yesterday morning, the police reported to the Second Special Court. Prosecutor Lou Guangguan and the forensic scribe came to the office to verify that the deceased had committed suicide by hanging. Recent News of the Shangtuan Chinese Team 164

The Chinese team of the International Shangtuan has recently been very serious about various military training. At this time of crisis, the people of the whole country are all tragic and heroic, and their blood is boiling. The entire Chinese team in the field of military preparedness, in addition to righteous indignation, has all tended to enrich and actively prepare for breeding and training and to prepare for military preparedness. The following is the recent itinerary:

Expansion of Machine Guns The machine gun is the team's specialized subject. In the past, there were only four machine guns, and only two were used. Therefore, only a few dozen people in the left and right teams were proficient in this subject. Now, the officers of the team believe that the machine gun is an important subject in military affairs and should be popularized to expand training. Therefore, it has been expanded to eight machine guns. All team members, regardless of new or old, can join, so that each can practice. Therefore, recently, the teachers of the subject have been using the morning and evening space to open machine gun lectures in the Shangtuan training hall every day, teaching in separate classes.

The Whole Team is Busy Camping Camping is an important part of the Shangtuan's duties. Each team must hold it once a year. The Chinese team entered the camp yesterday, Friday, and will disband next Monday. The location is still in the barracks of the shooting range for three whole days and nights of concentrated training. It is said that this year's camping curriculum is heavier than in previous years. In addition to the team exercises, practicing the formation of the platoon when advancing, and using signs instead of passwords in the field, there are actual exercises such as charge, slash, and street fighting, as well as lectures on map forms, practicing various fast and slow gun postures, and how to use high and low piers as cover. The curriculum is specified by time, and each member is allocated, working day and night, with no rest for a moment. The camping task is also said to be busy.

The Preparatory Members Start Training The preparatory members recruited by the team this year are expected to be more than 400 people due to the situation, which is more than twice the quota. Among them, half of them were not admitted due to age, guarantee inconsistencies, and poor physical condition. About 200 people who passed the physical examination and examination will be trained on December 1st to impart preliminary military knowledge.

The Appeal of the Tenants of Yixin Lane 169

The tenants of Yixin Lane on Nanjing Road, due to unreasonable oppression and forced relocation by landlords Cheng Linsheng and Cheng Yize, once sent representatives to petition the local party and government authorities, as reported in previous newspapers. Yesterday, the tenants submitted another petition to the Central Party Headquarters, the National Government, and relevant departments, requesting assistance. The original text stated: "We, the citizens, lease houses in and around Yixin Lane on Nanjing Road in the Shanghai Special District for business and residence, only for ten years. Suddenly, we were unreasonably forced to relocate by landlords Cheng Linsheng and Cheng Yize, great landlords, and were sued in court. Although the rights and wrongs should be quietly awaiting the court's decision, we dare not disturb your hearing. However, there are things we cannot refrain from saying and dare to present to your esteemed presence. According to the custom of renting houses in Shanghai, if the landlord wants the tenant to move out, one of the following facts must be present: (1) The house is damaged to the extent that it is uninhabitable and must be rebuilt; (2) The tenant has defaulted on rent for more than three months without reason. Now, the houses in this lane have only been built for ten years and are as good as new, so there is no need to rebuild them. The residents pay rent monthly and have never been in arrears, so there is no reason to force them to move out. Although Article 450, Paragraph 2 of the Civil Code stipulates that for contracts without a fixed term, each party may terminate the contract at any time, it clearly states that if there is a custom that is beneficial to the lessee, that custom should be followed. Now that Shanghai has a custom that is beneficial to the lessee, the lessee of the house should be protected by law. Moreover, Article 148 of the Civil Code stipulates that the exercise of rights must not be primarily for the purpose of harming others. Now, we, the citizens, lease the houses in this lane and have invested huge amounts of small rents and renovations, and some have even built three-story houses with the landlord's consent. Some were forced to relocate just one month after moving in. This kind of loss is truly incalculable. The landlord only considers the exercise of his own private interests and disregards the harm to others.

Page 16

Sun Yat-sen's principle of people's livelihood in his posthumous works discusses the land issue in detail. The key point is that the increase in land value is due to the labor of the public, and the landlord enjoys the benefits without working, which is equivalent to gaining without labor. Therefore, he advocates equalizing land rights. If the behavior of the landlord Cheng Linsheng, the great landlord, only considers his own interests and disregards the labor of the public, it is clearly a violation of Sun Yat-sen's teachings and goes against the purpose of building the country for the benefit of the people. The impact is immeasurable. Therefore, for the sake of maintaining public interests, respecting the law, and strictly following Sun Yat-sen's teachings, we dare not avoid the axe and risk our lives to state our case. We implore you to have mercy on the people's livelihood and hardship and quickly provide relief so that we citizens will not suffer from not having a place to live and do business, and the merchants and residents of the entire city will not be affected by Cheng Linsheng's actions. We citizens would be fortunate, and the citizens of Shanghai would be fortunate. Sincerely bowed by the residents of Yixin Lane on Nanjing Road, Shanghai Special District."

The Old Beauty trademark dispute, which has been unresolved for many years, is still pending. It is now known that the decision issued by the Executive Yuan regarding the Old Beauty trademark has been appealed by the Old Beauty Tobacco Company. The National Government has approved it to be submitted to the Administrative Court for review after it is established. Therefore, the decision previously issued by the Executive Yuan cannot be finalized before the Administrative Court is established and reviewed.

Zhang Shanzi and Zhang Daqian, brothers, famous calligraphers and painters, are well-known in the art world. They returned to Jianping, their hometown, this autumn, and have been separated from the people of Shanghai for a long time. It is now heard that the Zhang brothers detoured through Huangshan on their way back, enjoying the scenery of the thirty-six peaks, staying for a month. Now they have returned to Shanghai, and their works are even more detached, profound, and serene. All the accumulated commissions for calligraphy and painting in Shanghai will be cleared one by one.

The seventh issue of China Pictorial Magazine, known for its rigorous editing and rich content, has now been published. The paintings and photographs published are all from the hands of famous artists in the art world, and are even more exquisite than previous issues. There are large numbers of photos published on the continued occupation of the Northeast by violent Japan and the progress of the domestic peaceful reunification movement. In terms of text, Zhou Shoujuan's boycott of Japanese goods and Lu Dingkui's article on the Northeast Incident and International Law are particularly insightful and profound. Among them, the most rare photos, such as the practice of various novel weapons by students of American military schools and the various strange customs of the world's mysterious islands, are the special features of this issue. In addition, there are ancient Buddhist artifacts from India, the contents of Tibet, domestic and international current affairs, the actual situation of the national salvation movement in various provinces, recent photos of famous ladies, the giant beasts of the Hamburg Zoo in Germany, the three-color printed "Autumn Mountain Exploration" by Hu Boxiang, the art paper printed "After the Rain" by Zhang Zhenhou, Wu Shixian's "Autumn Mountain Rain Clearing", new school paintings from Europe, as well as modern home furnishings, a glimpse of the domestic paint manufacturing process, and so on, are all valuable works. The texts include Zhang Ziping's long masterpiece "Between Man and Beast", the pessimistic monk's "Footprints in the Buddhist Country", Ms. Shi Qu's "What I Hope for China", Ms. Jin Yu's "A Glimpse of Chrysanthemum Cultivation", etc. The general distributor is the New China Bookstore at the intersection of Haining Road and North Sichuan Road in Shanghai, and major bookstores are selling it. Each issue is priced at four dimes of ocean, plus one for postage. It is said that they still need to recruit managers from other places. Those who are willing to take on the job can directly contact the company.

A Summary of the Economic Situation in the Three Northeastern Provinces Reprinted 176

The book "A Summary of the Economic Situation in the Three Northeastern Provinces" is a carefully researched work by Lian Jun, who was sent to the Eastern Provinces by the Overseas Chinese Industrial Society to investigate. The book analyzes and describes the waxing and waning of Japanese and Russian forces, and provides detailed information on the agricultural, industrial, commercial, forestry, mining, railway, financial, and immigration conditions of the region, totaling fifteen chapters, with forty-four appendices, detailing various secret treaties, treaties, agreements, contracts, edicts, memorials, exchange notes, records, meeting minutes, etc. The entire book contains more than 300,000 words, with more than 150 illustrations, charts, photos, and maps. The second edition of the book has been published, exquisitely printed in one thick volume, priced at a special price of one yuan and eight dimes per volume. The Commercial Press and major bookstores are selling it on consignment.

Declaration of Unemployed Workers of Dahua Factory 179

Declaration of all unemployed workers of Dahua Industrial Factory: "Since violent Japan has been rampant and occupied the Eastern Provinces, hearing the news makes our blood boil and tears flow. We colleagues' patriotic enthusiasm dares not lag behind. Therefore, we have specially organized an Anti-Japanese National Salvation Association, hoping to pledge to save the country under the guidance of the Central Government and make unremitting efforts. However, since the organization is just beginning, everything needs economy. We have repeatedly laid bare the pros and cons to the factory, earnestly requesting assistance and generously allocating subsidies. The factory also agreed to provide strong support because it involved patriotic movement and was a matter of righteousness. We colleagues secretly celebrated that the funds were available and the anti-Japanese work could move forward unimpeded. After a few days, we colleagues, seeing that the funds for anti-Japanese activities were in urgent need, went to the factory to collect them. Unexpectedly, the factory owner Shao Daren was cunning by nature and changed his original intention, suddenly going back on his word, pointing out that organizing anti-Japanese national salvation was a preposterous move, and recklessly ignoring everything, stopping the factory for no reason. His actions of acting as an accomplice for the enemy and helping tyranny are openly sabotaging the anti-Japanese movement and are already outrageous. Moreover, suddenly announcing the closure of the factory disregards the livelihoods of more than 240 workers and is an extremely sinister trick that no capitalist has ever used. Later, he even went further, instigating Cheng Yusheng, the director of the materials department, to beat and injure more than a dozen workers to sell his tactics of armed oppression. We colleagues have repeatedly appealed to the party and government organs for fair assistance, and they have all ordered the resumption of work, but the factory has repeatedly delayed and insisted on not allowing it, and its ulterior motives are obvious. Since the factory stopped work, it has been a month. We colleagues' livelihoods have been exhausted, and we are all in a state of turmoil and displacement. If the factory continues to insist and unreasonably refuses, then the workers have no way to appeal and no way to implement. We have no choice but to gamble with the heads of all the workers. If the factory takes the dismissal of representatives as a condition for starting work, it will be resolutely opposed by all the workers. We hope that all sectors will uphold justice, uphold public reason, and provide strong assistance. This is our declaration. We hope you will take note. (Issued on behalf of the Shanghai Postal Workers' Union)"

Fire in Yangjing Town 180

At the Zhao Azhao's house, who is a carpenter in Lingjia Wooden Bridge in the north of Yangjing Town in Pudong, a fire suddenly broke out in the kitchen at 0:30 this morning and immediately broke through the roof. Zhao's daughter-in-law, Pan, woke up from her sleep and saw that the door had been burned down. She hurriedly escaped through the back window. All the boxes and items were burned to ashes before they could be salvaged. When the fire was raging, Inspector Sui Xiangchen of Taikoo Dock led the police to the scene to help extinguish it. It is estimated that five houses and half a hall were burned, with losses of about seven or eight hundred gold. Afterwards, the police from the second branch of the third district ordered the police to bring Zhao's daughter-in-law, Pan, to the case for a brief questioning and sent her to the Public Security Bureau for interrogation. Unexpectedly, Pan fell to the ground in panic and became unconscious outside the gate of the town. The escorting police woke her up and returned to the office to report. Director Yao instructed her to be temporarily released on bail pending investigation of the cause of the fire.

News from Trade Associations 181

Paint and Woodware Industry: The Paint and Woodware Industry Association convened a general meeting of members at the Xuenongdi Clubhouse the day before yesterday afternoon. More than 200 members attended. The meeting was called to order at 3 o'clock. First, the chairman, Du Gengsheng, reported the purpose of the meeting. Then, the secretary, Min Xingchu, reported the progress of the past week, stating that since the reorganization of the association in October last year, all matters that the association should handle have been carried out step by step and without reservation: (1) Requesting the municipal government and the finance bureau to exempt the clubhouse from the four seasons' tax on houses; (2) Requesting various ministries and departments of the national government to reduce the business tax; (3) Requesting the party and government organs to change the name to the Paint and Woodware Industry Association and to rename the newly organized Chinese and Western Woodware Industry to Chinese and Western Furniture Industry; (4) Handling the filling of business tax forms for the six major industry groups; (5) Collecting donations for flood relief in various provinces on behalf of others; (6) Dispatching personnel to investigate whether the various industry groups were selling mixed Japanese raw materials and to uphold economic severance and permanent boycott; (7) Sending representatives to participate in the petition for peace to the Guangdong authorities stationed in Shanghai; (8) Actively carrying out the work of assisting Ma and resisting Japan. In addition, after reporting the official documents and letters and the brief report on income and expenditure of the past week item by item, two representatives from the higher-level authorities, He and Li, gave speeches on the various cruel and inhuman conditions of violent Japan towards the people of the Three Northeastern Provinces, which were unprecedented. They should ask the members present to uphold their conscience and step up anti-Japanese work. Next, the chairman announced that all industry groups that have not joined the association must join the association uniformly within the year, and the public fees to be collected will remain the same. If they still wait and see within the year, it is decided that from January next year, they will be collected in three grades of 20 yuan, 40 yuan, and 60 yuan in accordance with the resolutions passed at the inaugural meeting, and no more special considerations will be given. Next, Chen Yougeng, Ma Yunxiang, Xu Guoqing, and other members expressed their opinions on improving the association's affairs. Guest Lin Zhizhou spoke about various anti-Japanese works, emphasizing that all people must be of one mind and persevere to the end. His words were earnest, and everyone applauded and praised them. Finally, the chairman gave a thank-you speech, and the meeting was adjourned at six o'clock.

Barbering Industry: The Shanghai Barbering Industry Association specially convened an inaugural meeting yesterday afternoon at 2:00 p.m. More than 500 people attended. The chairman reported the purpose of the meeting and the preparations, and representatives from the municipal party headquarters gave instructions and passed the articles of association. The membership fee was amended and passed, with the membership fee divided into five types: (1) 8 yuan, (2) 6 yuan, (3) 4 yuan, (4) 2 yuan, (5) 1 yuan; the monthly fee was divided into five types: (1) 1 yuan, (2) 8 dimes, (3) 6 dimes, (4) 4 dimes, (5) 2 dimes. Finally, fifteen executive committee members were elected, and the meeting was adjourned.

Reader Letters

A Reader's Letter 183

(Speculating on Future Unified Response)

Japan's aggressive encroachment has roused national indignation. Your esteemed newspaper provides readers with an opportunity to express their anti-Japanese sentiments. As a soldier, I will present my limited views from a military standpoint for your guidance and request publication in your esteemed newspaper for national consideration. The fall of the Eastern Provinces and the League of Nations' inaction have led the people to advocate war with Japan. Given the current situation, our nation cannot survive without war, and Japan cannot fulfill its long-held ambitions without war. China and Japan are irreconcilable. It is like an arrow on the string, that must be released. Once war begins, given China's vast territory and large population, it would take Japan no less than ten years of arduous fighting and enormous military expenditures to conquer all of China. Even if Japan conquered all of China, our people would rise up in rebellion everywhere, and the Japanese army would be exhausted from constant fighting. Moreover, if Japan were to subjugate China, it would certainly arouse the great忌 (jealousy/disapproval) of the great powers. The Japanese must consider this carefully. Therefore, they will certainly not adopt the Yuan and Qing dynasties' method of conquering every city and town. In my opinion, at the beginning of the war, Japan will certainly use all of its naval, land, and air forces to occupy Tianjin, Beiping, Qingdao, Jinan, Haizhou, Shanghai, Nanjing, Hankou, Fuzhou, Guangzhou, and other important cities, blockade our ports, cut off our economy, and destroy our arsenals, so that we will have no way to replenish the arms and ammunition that are essential for combat. Then, they will entice and coerce second Xi Qia-types to organize a Chinese government under Japanese protection, provide them with arms and ammunition, and incite them to attack the national army in the interior, while they watch from across the river with indifference. Sixty years later, the so-called protected Chinese government will follow Korea into oblivion. Some might say that my worries are unfounded because Tianjin, Beiping, Qingdao, Shanghai, Nanjing, Hankou, Fuzhou, Guangzhou, and other places have a large number of foreign residents, and there are trade treaty relationships. Even if the Japanese are arrogant, they would not dare to risk incurring the wrath of the great powers by occupying them with military force. Moreover, our country is now united, and there will be no one willing to be a puppet like Xi Qia. I say that is not so. Let me cite examples to prove it. Did Shenyang not have foreign residents? Did the Japanese army not cross the Chinese Eastern Railway and invade Russia's sphere of influence when they occupied Qiqihar? Did the Japanese army's shelling of the Chinese areas in Tianjin not violate the trade treaties? We have not heard of the great powers preventing the Japanese from occupying Shenyang because of the foreign residents there. We have not heard of Soviet Russia expelling the Japanese army for invading its sphere of influence. We have not heard of the foreign troops stationed in Tianjin interfering with the Japanese army's shelling of the Chinese areas. Learning from the past, since the Japanese have been plotting to seize us, they will certainly use diplomatic means of maneuvering, enticing with sweet words and promises of sharing benefits, and making assurances that they will not invade the foreign concessions or harm the interests of the great powers, so that the great powers will turn a deaf ear and remain silent. Moreover, they can also argue to the great powers that "Japan has not invaded China. It is just that the current Chinese government is in constant internal strife, and the people are suffering. Japan, out of concern for its neighbors, has no choice but to help the enlightened people of China to organize a strong government to unify China." The great powers will probably not step forward to uphold justice and make things difficult for Japan if they do not suffer great losses themselves. As for saying that there will be no second Xi Qia, I say, I hope there will be none. However, in the past twenty years, the frustrated warlords and politicians, and the current greedy and power-hungry minority who hold military power and do not know what the country is, once they are coerced and enticed by the Japanese, I fear that there will not only be a second Xi Qia, but also a third, fourth, and countless Xi Qias. Now, summarizing the above discussion, if my words prove to be true, then our country must adopt a strategy of protracted war and be prepared for great sacrifices of people and resources in order to defeat the enemy. The following points are of utmost urgency: (1) We should actively prepare for war. Based on the above discussion, a war between China and Japan is inevitable, and the war will not be far off. Looking at Japan, they are gathering reservists, concentrating naval, land, and air forces, and organizing people's volunteer corps. Now, they are even using the excuse of insufficient government funds to issue bonds of 100 million to cover war expenses. They are poised for action and eager to try. Looking back at our country, according to newspaper reports, except for Guangzhou, where Chen Jitang once convened a meeting of generals and decided to concentrate troops and purchase more arms, other places are still singing and dancing, with no preparation. Troops have not been concentrated and deployed, and arms and ammunition have not been purchased or manufactured. What is even more puzzling is that at this time of national crisis, when we should be expanding our military and planning for war expenses, the Finance Committee is instead greatly reducing military spending, so that the existing troops are paid only 60% of their salaries, and no one is even mentioning the expansion of military equipment or the planning of war expenses. The newspapers are filled with impassioned telegrams from various groups, theoretical articles, and calls for war from the people, as if our people are all made of copper heads and iron arms, and can resist the Japanese warships and cannons with their bare hands. I fear that the pure discussion of Jin people will eventually lead to the chaos of the Five Barbarians invading China. At the beginning of the civil wars in the past, both sides recruited soldiers and expanded their armies, and did not hesitate to spend tens of millions of dollars to buy aircraft, artillery, and other weapons from foreign countries. All the arsenals were working day and night to produce ammunition. Now that a foreign war is imminent, these actions are nowhere to be seen, which is really puzzling. In my opinion, all other undertakings should be temporarily suspended, and the human and financial resources of the entire country should be concentrated on preparing for war. On the one hand, the existing naval and land forces should be mobilized to Tianjin, Beiping, Qingdao, Jinan, Haizhou, Shanghai, Nanjing, Hankou, Fuzhou, Guangzhou, and other places. We must seek decisive battles at the national borders and not seek battles in the interior until absolutely necessary. On the other hand, we should implement a compulsory conscription system and expand the army as much as possible (the current disaster victims can be selected first for the strong and formed into troops) to serve as the successors to the existing national army. On the other hand, we should raise huge sums of money to buy aircraft, artillery, tanks, anti-aircraft guns, and other weapons and ammunition materials from the great powers. On the other hand, we should order all arsenals to produce ammunition day and night, and all military equipment that can be manufactured. We must make the whole country soldiers, and everyone can fight. Only then can we talk about a protracted war. If our country can continue the war with Japan for more than two years, Japan will inevitably collapse and retreat. As for the volunteer corps organized in various places, in my opinion, they can be used to maintain order in the rear and encourage the people, but their effectiveness will be minimal if they meet the Japanese army on the battlefield. Because the experience, organization, command, economy, and other aspects of the volunteer corps cannot meet the requirements of actual combat. Young students should not be made to make unnecessary sacrifices unless absolutely necessary. Because these people are talents cultivated by the country for decades, and they are the backbone of the country's future development. If they are sent to the battlefield to sacrifice as soon as the war begins, the country will inevitably lack talent in everything after the victory and armistice. (2) Research on the ammunition problem. I believe that General Ma Zhanshan's withdrawal from Qiqihar was not due to exhaustion of food or lack of reinforcements, but to the exhaustion of ammunition. General Ma's telegram announcing the abandonment of Longjiang said, "After a day and night of fierce fighting, ammunition was exhausted. I had to retreat to Keshan to plan a counterattack." Alas, with General Ma's loyal, courageous, and skilled Black Army, defending a long battle line of more than a hundred miles could have been managed with ease. Even if the Japanese army's firearms were superior, the Black Army's spirit of internal unity could have resisted. However, from November 4 to November 19, after sixteen days of intense defensive battles, even if the Black Army had sufficient ammunition reserves, they would have been exhausted. If Zhang Xueliang and the central government could have supplied ammunition by air from the beginning of the war, I fear that the Japanese army would not be able to water their horses in Longjiang at this time. Speaking of this, let me also mention a strange thing, that is, Zhang Xueliang telegraphed Ma Zhanshan at the beginning of the war, instructing him to retreat to Heihe if necessary (see Shanghai News). Later, Ma Zhanshan fought bravely, but ammunition, salaries, and soldiers were not supplied. He was attacked by public opinion across the country. It was not until November 18 that he telegraphed the troops outside the pass, ordering them to be under Ma's command. What Zhang's intentions were is really incomprehensible. Based on the above facts, after the outbreak of war between China and Japan, the ammunition problem in our country is more important than any other problem. The largest arsenals in our country are Shenyang, Hanyang, Shanghai, Guangzhou, and Jinling, especially the Shenyang and Hanyang arsenals. The Shenyang arsenal has already been used by Zhang to help the enemy. Now, more than ten Japanese warships are concentrated in Hankou. I fear that their target must be the Hanyang arsenal. The arsenal is to the army as food and drink are to the human body. With the arsenal in place, it can continuously manufacture arms and ammunition to supply the army, so that we can talk about a protracted war. Once the war between China and Japan begins, the Japanese will certainly use all their naval and air forces to destroy the above arsenals. Then, will our country let it happen naturally and let them destroy them? Or will we find another way to protect the arsenals? In my opinion, our country should now purchase sufficient raw materials for ammunition and order the arsenals to process and manufacture them and transport them to the major military areas in the interior in preparation for a protracted war in the interior. If the government is confident of winning at the national border, it can build air defenses for the arsenals to prevent enemy aircraft from bombing them. If there is no such confidence, then the arsenals must be moved to the interior as soon as possible to avoid becoming a continuation of the Shenyang arsenal. (3) The people of the whole country should have the determination to sacrifice. Most of the people in our country are addicted to comfort and live for the moment. There are many A Dou who are happy and forget their homeland, and few Gou Jian who sleep on brushwood and taste gall. The Eastern Provinces have fallen. Look at the people of the Eastern Provinces, they are still living their lives for the moment. We have not heard of anyone fighting the Japanese with their lives. Today, the people in various parts of the country are indignant, but if they are occupied by the Japanese army, they will not be different from the people of the Eastern Provinces today, living their lives for the moment. Because the general mentality is that "I have elderly parents, I have beautiful wives, I have property, I have fields and houses. If the Japanese do not take them all away temporarily, why should I give up my life?" Alas, this is why India is not a country. Therefore, in my opinion, those who shout patriotism when the enemy is not at the border are not truly patriotic. Those who can fight the enemy with their lives when the enemy is at the border are truly patriotic. Our compatriots must today make a determination that "My life is already dead, but my country's life still exists. I will do everything I can to preserve this country's life." Then, we will not worry about the lack of successors when the war between China and Japan begins. Even if the war begins, and our military is at a disadvantage, Tianjin, Beiping, Qingdao, Jinan, Haizhou, Shanghai, Nanjing, Hankou, Fuzhou, Guangzhou, or other places are occupied by the enemy, the people of those places can abandon everything and move to the interior. If the enemy uses violence and threats to prevent them from moving, then they should fight the enemy army and traitors with their lives. At that time, no matter how cunning the Japanese invaders are and how treacherous the traitors are, they will have no way to cope. Today, the compatriots of the whole country must put life and death out of their minds, and everyone must have the idea of being certain to die, considering living as a disgrace and dying in battle as an honor. Only then can we talk about saving the country. As for how to make compatriots have this kind of determination, it depends on the efforts of the intellectuals to publicize it. In my opinion, the government must prepare for the above two items as soon as possible, so as to prevent the above-mentioned important places from suffering the sudden and unprepared fall of Shenyang. For the third item, the compatriots may not all have this ambition, so I offer my humble opinion for discussion.

(Reply) The plan is admirable, but the financial aspect is probably difficult to implement.

Weather Report 184

The Xujiahui Observatory's weather forecast at 4:30 PM yesterday stated that the Shandong coast and the Yangtze River basin will be cloudy and cold, with occasional rain or snow. The southern region will be sunny. There will be strong northwest to northeast winds over the Yellow Sea and East China Sea. Furthermore, the highest temperature in the city within the 24 hours before 3:00 PM yesterday was 52.7 degrees, and the lowest was 46.2 degrees. On the same day last year, the highest was 62.6 degrees, and the lowest was 42.3 degrees.

Letters to the Editor

To whom it may concern: According to the Qianjiang Guildhall, they were surprised to read in the news section of your newspaper on the 27th of this month that the Guildhall is planning to organize a silk and silk weaving limited company. After investigation, the Guildhall has no such intention, and there is no such organization in the industry. It is believed that the news is based on false rumors. Therefore, representatives have been entrusted to request a correction. We hereby inform you of the situation and request that you publish it in the "Letters to the Editor" section. With gratitude for your public service. Sincerely, Xi Yuchang, Lawyer, November 27th.

Dear Editor: In today's local news section of your newspaper, in the article "The County District Branches Urge Chiang to Go North," the phrase "each district branch" should be "the Second District Branch of the Second District of the County." We hereby inform you of this and request that you make a correction to avoid misunderstandings. With best regards, The Shanghai County Executive Committee of the Jiangsu Provincial Committee of the Chinese Kuomintang, November 27th.

To whom it may concern: We recently read an article in the local news section of your newspaper on November 27th regarding the People's National Salvation Association. The names of us are listed among the initiators. After investigating the content of the association, we were not aware of the situation beforehand, nor did we participate afterward. We hereby declare this and request that a correction be made. Sincerely, Wu Peiran and Liu Guanzhi, jointly.

Social News

Marshal Foch 185

European War Diary · Translated by Gu Angruo

That afternoon, the Versailles Conference continued to study the armistice treaty and decided to add conditions to the Russian front.

On the afternoon of November 2nd, there was another gathering in Versailles to discuss naval conditions and the Russian line provisions.

At the same time, the Supreme Commander of the Austrian Army received the armistice terms proposed by the Allied Powers from General Diez. What was the attitude of the Vienna government? Accept or reject? If accepted, would the disintegration of Austria-Hungary be sufficient to fulfill the conditions? The Allied authorities were quite hesitant about this issue. That afternoon, Mr. Lloyd George could not but abandon a large part of the demand for the surrender of German battleships.

After the Vienna government succumbed, he immediately put forward all the naval conditions again. He demanded that German battleships be disarmed and surrender multiple warships and submarines. The conditions were very harsh and difficult for the German army to accept. The land armistice terms also could not be signed as a result.

I asked the Allied governments to pay attention to the responsibility for continuing the bloodshed. The Allied governments then instructed me to include the naval conditions in the armistice terms, so that if the enemy could not accept the naval conditions, we could revise them.

In fact, the German army accepted everything.

The conditions on the Russian line and the Romanian front were accepted without discussion. Regarding this point, the French Foreign Minister Pichon raised the issue of the restoration of Poland, which was one of the war aims of the Allied forces. However, it was decided that this issue should not be mentioned in the same breath as the armistice issue. Now, it was only decided to demand that the German army in the east retreat to the original state in 1914.

On November 4th, the specific armistice terms were finally approved at the Versailles Conference. The leaders of the Allied governments immediately telegraphed President Wilson and decided that I, together with the British naval commander, would present these terms to the plenipotentiaries of the German government and be responsible for the negotiations.

When these terms were notified to Washington, the special envoy of the British government to the Allied governments reserved the principle of freedom of the seas among President Wilson's Fourteen Points.

I ordered the front-line soldiers to allow the German representatives to pass through the defensive lines to negotiate, while warning the troops to strictly guard against rumors.

At 12:30 AM on the night of November 6th, I received the first radio message from the German Supreme Command, notifying the names of the plenipotentiaries specially dispatched by the Berlin government and requesting that a meeting place be designated and whether a temporary ceasefire could be implemented when the German representatives arrived at the Allied lines.

I immediately replied simply, "If the German plenipotentiaries wish to meet Marshal Foch to request an armistice, they can go directly to a certain French military line. The guards have been ordered to escort them to the meeting place."

On the morning of the 7th, I learned that the German plenipotentiaries would depart from Spa at noon and arrive at the French military lines between 4:00 and 5:00 PM. The French and German armies prepared to cease fire when the German delegation passed through the fire line.

Together with Chief of Staff Weygand and three officers from the headquarters, and accompanied by the British naval representatives, I departed from Saint-Lyé by special train at 5:00 PM in the afternoon to meet the German plenipotentiaries in the Forest of Compiègne near Rethondes station.

Because the road in the German defense area was blocked, the German delegation did not arrive at the French military lines until 9:00 PM. They were twelve hours late to their destination. They did not arrive at the meeting place until 7:00 AM on November 8th.

The first negotiation was held at 9:00 AM in the French railway office car.

After the armistice treaty was signed, I reported the details of the Rethondes Conference between the Allied and German plenipotentiaries to the French President and Prime Minister. (Note: On November 8th, 1918, the negotiations began after the German representatives arrived. The Allied representatives were Marshal Foch, Chief of Staff Weygand, British Naval Commander Wemyss, Hope, and British Navy Captain Mari. The German representatives were Erzberger, Huf von Waldaorf, General Winterfeldt, Navy Captain Vanselow, Colonel Gatcher, and Colonel Heldor. The negotiations lasted for three days. The German side tried their best to reduce Foch's conditions. The German delegation repeatedly consulted with Berlin via radio. At 2:05 AM on the morning of November 11th, 1918, the German delegation notified Foch that they were ready to sign. At 2:15 AM, the final meeting was held. Chief of Staff Weygand read the armistice terms. At 5:05 AM, the terms were finalized. At 5:10 AM, the terms were signed. The German representatives withdrew. Marshal Foch immediately issued a radio message to the entire line, ordering a ceasefire at 11:00 AM.)

At 11:00 AM on the morning of November 11th, the Allied forces ceased fire on the entire line. The great war lasted fifty-three weeks, and the guns were now silent. The world began to see the hope of peace again.

The next day, I issued a victory message to the Allied forces as follows:

Soldiers of the Allied Forces,

You fought hard for months to repel the enemy and then attacked the enemy with indomitable spirit and unwavering determination.

You have won the greatest war in history and saved the most sacred ideals, the freedom of the world.

You deserve to be proud of your achievements.

You have gained immortal glory and eternal praise.

Commander-in-Chief of the Allied Forces, Foch (To be continued)
